href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane seasons</a><br />\n<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a>, <b>2017</b>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">2018</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">2019</a></i></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The <b>2017 Pacific hurricane season</b> is an ongoing event in the annual cycle of tropical cyclone formation, in which tropical cyclones form in the northeastern Pacific Ocean. The season officially started on May&#160;15 in the eastern Pacific, and on June&#160;1 in the central Pacific; they will both end on November&#160;30.<sup id="cite_ref-season_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-season-1">[1]</a></sup> These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">basin</a>. However, the formation of tropical cyclones is possible at any time of the year. This was demonstrated when the first storm, Tropical Storm Adrian, was <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named</a> on May&#160;10, and became the earliest-known tropical storm in the East Pacific since the advent of satellite imagery. Thus far, the season has seen near-average activity in terms of <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">ACE</a>, in stark contrast to the extremely active seasons in <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a>. For the first time since <a href="/wiki/2012_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2012 Pacific hurricane season">2012</a>, no tropical cyclones have formed in the Central Pacific.</p>\n<p>Beginning this year, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> has the option to issue advisories, and thus allow watches and warnings to be issued, on disturbances that are not yet tropical cyclones but have a high chance to become one, and are expected to bring tropical storm or hurricane conditions to landmasses within 48&#160;hours. Such systems are termed "potential tropical cyclones". Advisories on these storms contain the same content, including track forecasts and cyclone watches and warnings, as advisories on active tropical cyclones.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This was first demonstrated on August&#160;29 with the designation of Potential Tropical Cyclone Fourteen-E\xe2\x80\x94which later developed into <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)">Tropical Storm Lidia</a>\xe2\x80\x94south-southeast of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a />\nhurricanes</th>\n<th>Ref</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>EPAC</td>\n<td>17</td>\n<td>9</td>\n<td>4</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>CPAC</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td>0</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2"><b>Actual activity</b>:</td>\n<td>17</td>\n<td>9</td>\n<td>4</td>\n<td></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On May&#160;25, 2017, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> released its annual forecast, predicting a 80% chance of a near- to above-average season in both the Eastern and Central Pacific basins, with a total of 14\xe2\x80\x9320 named storms, 6\xe2\x80\x9311 hurricanes, and 3\xe2\x80\x937 major hurricanes.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-5">[5]</a></sup> During May 28, the <a href="/wiki/Servicio_Meteorol%C3%B3gico_Nacional" class="mw-redirect" title="Servicio Meteorol\xc3\xb3gico Nacional">Servicio Meteorol\xc3\xb3gico Nacional</a> (SMN) issued its first forecast for the season, predicting a total of 16 named storms, 10 hurricanes and 6 major hurricanes to develop.<sup id="cite_ref-SMN_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMN-6">[6]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2017_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2017 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2017 Pacific hurricane season</a></div>\n<center>\n<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_bdbbd120676b72e11fecbb4b975bdb96" id="timeline_bdbbd120676b72e11fecbb4b975bdb96">\n<area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" coords="452,64,516,84" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)" alt="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)" />\n<area shape="rect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" coords="602,198,761,218" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale" alt="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale" /></map><img usemap="#timeline_bdbbd120676b72e11fecbb4b975bdb96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/bdbbd120676b72e11fecbb4b975bdb96.png" /></div>\n</center>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" class="mw-redirect" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) for the 2017 Pacific hurricane season, as of Ramon\'s final advisory, is 97.39&#160;units (96.4575&#160;units from the East Pacific and 0.9325&#160;units from the Central Pacific).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[nb 2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Although the East Pacific hurricane season does not officially begin until May&#160;15, activity began several days prior with the formation of a tropical depression on May&#160;9. This marked the earliest formation of a tropical cyclone in the basin, surpassing <a href="/wiki/1990_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Alma" title="1990 Pacific hurricane season">1990\'s Hurricane Alma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Adrianrecord_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adrianrecord-9">[7]</a></sup> It intensified into Tropical Storm Adrian a few hours later, marking the earliest formation of a named storm on record.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> Near normal activity occurred in June, with Tropical Storm Calvin formed on June 11, and Hurricane Dora on June 25<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> the following month was well above average; July featured the fifth-highest ACE value on record and boosted the seasonal value to almost double that of the long-term average.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup> This total was attributed to long lived hurricanes Eugene, Fernanda, Hilary and Irwin. August saw less activity, but did feature Category 4 Hurricane Kenneth and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Lidia">Tropical Storm Lidia</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Adrian">Tropical Storm Adrian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Adrian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Adrian 2017-05-09 1912Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/150px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg" width="150" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/225px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg/300px-Adrian_2017-05-09_1912Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1002" data-file-height="1302" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Adrian_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Adrian 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/150px-Adrian_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/225px-Adrian_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Adrian_2017_track.png/300px-Adrian_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>May 9&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 May 11</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1004&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Pacific hurricanes">List of off-season Pacific hurricanes</a></div>\n<p>On May&#160;5, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) indicated that an <a href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Low pressure area">area of low pressure</a> was forecast to form south of Mexico over subsequent days, with the possibility of tropical cyclone development thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> A broad <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_circulation" title="Atmospheric circulation">cyclonic circulation</a> began to develop as expected late on May&#160;7,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> gradually organizing into the season\'s first tropical depression by 21:00&#160;UTC on May&#160;9.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> Upon formation, at which point it was located about 545&#160;mi (875&#160;km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">Salina Cruz, Mexico</a>, the depression became the earliest-forming East Pacific tropical cyclone (east of 140\xc2\xb0W) on record. The previous record was held by <a href="/wiki/1990_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Alma" title="1990 Pacific hurricane season">1990\'s Hurricane Alma</a>, which formed on May 12.<sup id="cite_ref-Adrianrecord_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adrianrecord-9">[7]</a></sup> The depression intensified into Tropical Storm Adrian six hours later, the earliest-known formation of a named storm in eastern Pacific proper since the advent of the satellite era.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> Initially, forecasts expected the small storm to intensify into a powerful hurricane. Shortly after reaching peak intensity early on May 10, an unexpected increase in mid-level <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> caused Adrian to quickly weaken back to a tropical depression by 03:00&#160;UTC on May 11.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> Early on the next day, Adrian degenerated into a remnant low.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Beatriz">Tropical Storm Beatriz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Beatriz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Beatriz 2017-06-01 1710Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/150px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg" width="150" height="195" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/225px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg/300px-Beatriz_2017-06-01_1710Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="7800" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Beatriz_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Beatriz 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/150px-Beatriz_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/225px-Beatriz_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Beatriz_2017_track.png/300px-Beatriz_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>May 31&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 June 2</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1001&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A tropical wave emerged off the western coast of Africa on May&#160;18 and entered the East Pacific about a week later, where steady organization led to the formation of a tropical depression around 12:00&#160;UTC on May&#160;31. Embedded within southwesterly flow around a large upper-level trough across northern Mexico, the depression moved steadily northeast in a favorable environment, and it intensified into Tropical Storm Beatriz by 06:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;1. After attaining peak winds of 45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h), the system made landfall around 00:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;2 about 25&#160;miles (40&#160;km) west of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_%C3%81ngel" title="Puerto \xc3\x81ngel">Puerto \xc3\x81ngel</a>. The mountainous terrain of Mexico quickly disrupted Beatriz, and it ultimately dissipated twelve hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-Btcr_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Btcr-19">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the state of <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">Oaxaca</a>, flights out of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADas_de_Huatulco_International_Airport" title="Bah\xc3\xadas de Huatulco International Airport">Bah\xc3\xadas de Huatulco International Airport</a> were cancelled, and schools were closed until at least June&#160;3. Dozens of roads were rendered impassable due to mudslides and flooding; numerous locales received over 4&#160;in (102&#160;mm) of rain, with a storm total of 19.07&#160;in (484.4&#160;mm) in <a href="/wiki/Huatulco" title="Huatulco">Huatulco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Btcr_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Btcr-19">[17]</a></sup> Numerous <a href="/wiki/Landslides" class="mw-redirect" title="Landslides">landslides</a> caused significant disruption across the state, especially by blocking <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Federal_Highway_200" title="Mexican Federal Highway 200">Federal Highway 200</a> at many areas. A landslide in <a href="/wiki/San_Marcial_Ozolotepec" title="San Marcial Ozolotepec">San Marcial Ozolotepec</a> killed two girls and buried several houses, while another in <a href="/wiki/San_Carlos_Yautepec" title="San Carlos Yautepec">San Carlos Yautepec</a> killed a woman.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> As of June 4, a total of seven people have been killed\xe2\x80\x94five in Oaxaca and two in <a href="/wiki/Tehuantepec" title="Tehuantepec">Tehuantepec</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> Less than two weeks after Beatriz, Tropical Storm Calvin affected similar areas of Mexico and inflicted additional damage. Combined damage from the two systems reached at least 70&#160;million pesos (US$3.9&#160;million) in Oaxaca.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Calvin">Tropical Storm Calvin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Calvin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Calvin 2017-06-12 2000Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/150px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg" width="150" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/225px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg/300px-Calvin_2017-06-12_2000Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5600" data-file-height="7200" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Calvin_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Calvin 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/150px-Calvin_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/225px-Calvin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Calvin_2017_track.png/300px-Calvin_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 11&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 June 13</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1004&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>In the second week of June, the NHC forecast the development of a broad area of low pressure a few hundred miles south of Mexico over the next several days.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup> This prediction came to fruition on June&#160;9,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> and the fledgling disturbance steadily organized into a tropical depression by 12:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;11 while located about 150&#160;mi (240&#160;km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">Salina Cruz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> It was slow to organize initially amid moderate easterly wind shear as it drifted northwestwards;<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> by 18:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;12, however, the tropical depression intensified into Tropical Storm Calvin.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> Intensifying slightly to reach winds of 45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h),<sup id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> Calvin made <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfall</a> halfway between Salina Cruz and Puerto \xc3\x81ngel, near Paja Blanca, around 00:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;13.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> Just 12&#160;hours later, Calvin dissipated into a remnant low.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup> The remnants of the storm caused heavy rainfall and some flooding in the area,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> however no fatalities were reported.<sup id="cite_ref-Ctcr_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ctcr-25">[23]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Dora">Hurricane Dora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hurricane Dora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Dora 2017-06-26 2020Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/150px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg" width="150" height="203" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/225px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg/300px-Dora_2017-06-26_2020Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8021" data-file-height="10859" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Dora_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Dora 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/150px-Dora_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/225px-Dora_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Dora_2017_track.png/300px-Dora_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>June 25&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 June 28</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 981&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On June&#160;21, the NHC began monitoring a broad area of low pressure south of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tehuantepec" title="Gulf of Tehuantepec">Gulf of Tehuantepec</a> for possible tropical cyclogenesis.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> The disturbance organized into a tropical depression by 03:00&#160;UTC on June&#160;25,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> and became a tropical storm six hours later, receiving the name <i>Dora</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> Progressing in a west-northwesterly direction at a steady speed, the storm began a 30-hour period of rapid intensification and became the first hurricane of the season at 09:00 UTC on June 26.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> With impressive upper-level outflow and an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> apparent on satellite imagery,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> the storm attained peak winds of 90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h) by late on June&#160;26.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> Dora maintained its intensity for a number of hours before beginning to rapidly weaken over cooler sea surface temperatures and in an environment of drier air.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> The storm later degenerated into a remnant low early on June 28, after all of the storm\'s deep convection had dissipated.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The outer bands of Dora brought heavy rains to <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a>, resulting in flash floods that inundated 20&#160;homes. Overall damage was minor, however.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Eugene">Hurricane Eugene</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hurricane Eugene">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Eugene 2017-07-09 1815Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg/150px-Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg" width="150" height="198" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg/225px-Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg/300px-Eugene_2017-07-09_1815Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5066" data-file-height="6679" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Eugene_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Eugene 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eugene_2017_track.png/150px-Eugene_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eugene_2017_track.png/225px-Eugene_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Eugene_2017_track.png/300px-Eugene_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 7&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 12</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 966&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Hurricane Eugene developed from a disturbance located 765&#160;mi (1,230&#160;km) south of the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> on July 7.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> On the following day, Eugene underwent a period of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>; in an 18-hour period starting at 21:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;8, Eugene intensified from a tropical storm with 70&#160;mph (110&#160;km/h) winds to a Category&#160;3 hurricane with 115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) winds, making it the first major hurricane of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> However, by 12 hours later, the entrainment of dry air caused Eugene to weaken to a Category&#160;2 hurricane,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> and due to traveling over cooler waters, Eugene weakened to a tropical storm on the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> As the coverage of deep convection steadily dwindled, Eugene fell to tropical depression intensity around 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;12 and degenerated to a remnant low six hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Dangerous <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">rip currents</a> combined with swells of 4 to 8&#160;ft (1.2 to 2.4&#160;m) across southern California resulted in hundreds of rescues. On July&#160;10 alone, lifeguards in <a href="/wiki/Huntington_Beach,_California" title="Huntington Beach, California">Huntington Beach</a> made 200&#160;rescues while 600 were made in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a>; lifeguards also responded to 700&#160;medical emergencies.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Fernanda">Hurricane Fernanda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hurricane Fernanda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Fernanda 2017-07-14 2135Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/150px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg" width="150" height="201" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/225px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg/300px-Fernanda_2017-07-14_2135Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5796" data-file-height="7757" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Fernanda_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Fernanda 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/150px-Fernanda_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/225px-Fernanda_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Fernanda_2017_track.png/300px-Fernanda_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 12&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 22</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>145&#160;mph (230&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 947&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Late on July&#160;10, the NHC began monitoring a broad area of low pressure several hundred miles southwest of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Colima" title="Manzanillo, Colima">Manzanillo</a>. Contrary to predictions of gradual development,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> the disturbance rapidly organized into a tropical depression by 03:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;12,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> and further strengthened to become Tropical Storm Fernanda around 15:00&#160;UTC that day.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> The nascent cyclone initially battled moderate northeasterly wind shear, with its low-level circulation displaced to the northeastern edge of the deep convection.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> This period of unfavorable upper-level winds was short-lived, and soon afterwards Fernanda commenced a period of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>, intensifying into a hurricane at 21:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;13.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> A well-defined eye formed within a growing <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a>, and Fernanda further intensified into a major hurricane early on July 14.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> Only six hours later, the system was upgraded to a Category 4 hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> At 10.9\xc2\xb0N, Fernanda became the second strongest hurricane to occur at such a low latitude in the Eastern Pacific, only behind <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Olaf" title="2015 Pacific hurricane season">2015\'s Hurricane Olaf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<p>With expansive upper-level outflow and spiral bands, a distinct eye, and a symmetric central dense overcast, Fernanda attained peak winds of 145&#160;mph (230&#160;km/h) around 03:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;15.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> A series of microwave passes around that time began to indicate the formation of a secondary eyewall that halted the cyclone\'s development as it tracked west-northwest to northwest.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> The eyewall replacement cycle concluded early on July&#160;16, allowing Fernanda to remain a powerful hurricane amid favorable environmental conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> By late on July&#160;18, however, cooler ocean temperatures and a more stable environment prompted the storm\'s weakening trend.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> Fernanda fell below hurricane intensity shortly before entering the Central Pacific as it succumbed to stronger southwesterly wind shear,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> and after failing to produce sustained deep convection, degenerated to a remnant low about 500&#160;miles (805&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Hilo,_Hawaii" title="Hilo, Hawaii">Hilo, Hawaii</a>, by 21:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;22.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Greg">Tropical Storm Greg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Greg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Greg 2017-07-21 1835Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/150px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg" width="150" height="192" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/225px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg/300px-Greg_2017-07-21_1835Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4417" data-file-height="5665" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Greg Pacific 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/150px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/225px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png/300px-Greg_Pacific_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 17&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 26</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>60&#160;mph (95&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1001&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On July&#160;12, the NHC forecast the formation of a broad area of low pressure south of Mexico over subsequent days.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> The disturbance formed two days later and slowly organized into a tropical depression by 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;17.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> The cyclone battled strong west-northwesterly wind shear after formation, intensifying into Tropical Storm Greg by 09:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;18 as deep convection burst near the center, but remained steady state for several days thereafter despite continued predictions of intensification.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> Ultimately, given global models\' poor handling of the environment, NHC lowered their intensity forecast for Greg.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> The cyclone continued west for the remainder of its life and maintained a similar convective structure, with intermittent bursts of deep convection near the center.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Approaching the Central Pacific, Greg\'s low-level circulation became increasingly difficult to locate as it moved into a cooler, drier environment intertwined by increasing southerly wind shear, and the system weakened to a tropical depression around 21:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;25.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> It degenerated to a remnant low 24 hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eight-E">Tropical Depression Eight-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eight-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="08E 2017-07-18 1805Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/150px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg" width="150" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/225px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg/300px-08E_2017-07-18_1805Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1084" data-file-height="1376" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:08E_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="08E 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/150px-08E_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/225px-08E_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/08E_2017_track.png/300px-08E_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 18&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35&#160;mph (55&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1007&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>A low-pressure trough began producing disorganized convection over the waters of the Pacific Ocean, well to the south of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, on July&#160;14.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Despite only marginally conducive environmental conditions, the disturbance began to show signs of organization two days later,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> and it attained tropical depression status by 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;18.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> Strong west-northwesterly <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> confined the storm\'s intermittent bursts of convection well to the southwest of its low-level circulation, and the depression consequently failed to produce winds above 35&#160;mph (55&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> The system\'s center later degenerated into a low-pressure trough within the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a>, prompting the NHC to discontinue advisories at 21:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Hilary">Hurricane Hilary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Hilary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hilary 2017-07-25 2015Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/150px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg" width="150" height="187" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/225px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg/300px-Hilary_2017-07-25_2015Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5140" data-file-height="6393" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Hilary_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Hilary 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/150px-Hilary_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/225px-Hilary_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Hilary_2017_track.png/300px-Hilary_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 21&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 31</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>105&#160;mph (165&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 972&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Part of an exceptionally active July, the NHC began highlighting the far eastern reaches of the Pacific basin on July&#160;19 for tropical development in later days.<sup id="cite_ref-Daniel_P._Brown_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_P._Brown-74">[72]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather progressed westward across <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> later that day,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> steadily organizing into a tropical depression by 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;21.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> The cyclone failed to organize immediately after formation, and its low-level center migrated to the southern extent of associated convection.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> By 03:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;23, though, better defined banding features and a more organized convective structure led the NHC to designate the system as Tropical Storm Hilary.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Over the coming hours, the cyclone\'s convective structure evolved into a small central dense overcast while hints of an eye became apparent;<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> in accordance with satellite estimates, Hilary was upgraded to a hurricane at 09:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;24.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> A moist environment and warm ocean waters propelled Hilary to its peak as a Category&#160;2 hurricane with winds of 105&#160;mph (165&#160;km/h) 24 hours later, at which time its core was most symmetric.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> After maintaining its intensity, the hurricane began to weaken late on July&#160;26 as northerly wind shear increased.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> It fell back to tropical storm intensity around 03:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;27 and ultimately degenerated to a remnant low four days later.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Irwin">Hurricane Irwin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hurricane Irwin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Irwin 2017-07-25 2120Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/150px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg" width="150" height="186" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/225px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg/300px-Irwin_2017-07-25_2120Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8093" data-file-height="10039" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Irwin_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Irwin 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/150px-Irwin_2017_track.png" width="150" height="95" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/225px-Irwin_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Irwin_2017_track.png/300px-Irwin_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1907" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>July 22&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 1</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 980&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On July&#160;16, the NHC highlighted the expected formation of an area of low pressure south of Mexico later that week.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> A tropical wave began producing disorganized cloudiness three days later,<sup id="cite_ref-Daniel_P._Brown_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_P._Brown-74">[72]</a></sup> and the broad system slowly organized into a tropical depression by 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;22.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Its structure changed little after formation, impinged by strong wind shear; despite this, satellite wind data indicated the cyclone intensified into Tropical Storm Irwin by 09:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;23.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> Over the next 24 hours, deep convection began to wrap around the center and a mid-level eye formed as environmental conditions improved;<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> by 09:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;25, Irwin intensified into a hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Although coolest cloudtops were located in the western semicircle of the system, a well-defined eye and convection in the eyewall propelled Irwin to its peak with winds of 90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h) late on July&#160;25.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Almost immediately, outflow from nearby Hurricane Hilary increased wind shear over the system and caused it to begin weakening;<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> Irwin rapidly fell to tropical storm strength around 15:00&#160;UTC on July&#160;26.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> Contrary to projections of continued weakening, however, the storm\'s cloud pattern maintained or even improved over subsequent days as it passed over marginal ocean temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> Finally, after losing its deep convection and being reduced to a swirl of low-level clouds, Irwin was declared a remnant low around 21:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;1.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eleven-E">Tropical Depression Eleven-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eleven-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="11E 2017-08-04 2015Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/150px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg" width="150" height="203" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/225px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg/300px-11E_2017-08-04_2015Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4577" data-file-height="6193" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:11E_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="11E 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/150px-11E_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/225px-11E_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/11E_2017_track.png/300px-11E_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 4&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>35&#160;mph (55&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1004&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On July&#160;28, the NHC advertised the likely development of an area of low pressure well south of Mexico over subsequent days.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> An area of disorganized showers and thunderstorms associated with a tropical wave materialized three days later, but little change occurred thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> Early on August&#160;3, a surface circulation formed in association with concentrating convection,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> and this process led to the formation of a tropical depression by 15:00&#160;UTC the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> The newly formed cyclone did not intensify after designation, and its low- and mid-level circulations separated by over 265&#160;mi (425&#160;km) on August&#160;5.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> Falling short of the tropical cyclone criteria, the short-lived depression was declared a remnant low at 21:00&#160;UTC that day.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Jova">Tropical Storm Jova</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Jova">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Jova 2017-08-11 Suomi NPP.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg" width="150" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Jova_2017-08-11_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2161" data-file-height="2862" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Jova_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Jova 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/150px-Jova_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/225px-Jova_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Jova_2017_track.png/300px-Jova_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 12&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 14</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>40&#160;mph (65&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1003&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The NHC began monitoring a strong tropical wave over the eastern Caribbean on August&#160;3.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> The feature pushed westward, developing into <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin" title="Hurricane Franklin">Hurricane Franklin</a> before making landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n" title="Yucat\xc3\xa1n">Yucat\xc3\xa1n</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> and attaining its peak as a Category&#160;1 hurricane before making landfall near <a href="/wiki/Vega_de_Alatorre" title="Vega de Alatorre">Vega de Alatorre, Veracruz</a> on August&#160;10.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> Although its low-level circulation dissipated, the NHC in days prior noted the potential for Franklin\'s mid-level remnants to reform in the East Pacific.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The remnants of Franklin induced a surface low off the coast of southwestern Mexico on August&#160;11, and steady organization led to the formation of Tropical Storm Jova by 03:00&#160;UTC the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> On a westward course, Jova was plagued by strong wind shear from an area of high pressure over northwestern Mexico, with a very disorganized appearance on satellite.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> After lacking sufficient organization to be declared a tropical cyclone, the storm was declared a remnant low around 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;14.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kenneth">Hurricane Kenneth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Hurricane Kenneth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kenneth 2017-08-20 2156Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/150px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg" width="150" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/225px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg/300px-Kenneth_2017-08-20_2156Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6077" data-file-height="8771" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Kenneth_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Kenneth 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/150px-Kenneth_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/225px-Kenneth_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kenneth_2017_track.png/300px-Kenneth_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 18&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 August 23</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>130&#160;mph (215&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 952&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On August&#160;12, the NHC noted the potential for an area of low pressure to form well south of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> during the following days.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather developed two days later as predicted;<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> however, organization was slow to occur, and a tropical depression only formed four days later, around 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;18.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> The newly formed cyclone embarked on a west to west-northwest course, intensifying into Tropical Storm Kenneth early on August&#160;19 and further into a hurricane by 15:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> Despite forecasts of only slight additional intensification,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> Kenneth rapidly intensified, with the <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye feature</a> warming dramatically and the surrounding cloud tops cooling. The cyclone attained <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">major hurricane</a> strength around 03:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;21,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> and six hours later reached its peak as a Category&#160;4 hurricane with sustained winds of 130&#160;mph (215&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Progressively cooler <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> and increasing <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a> caused Kenneth to steadily weaken following the intensification trend, with its inner core eroding and low-level circulation becoming displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> By 21:00&#160;UTC on August&#160;22, the storm weakened below hurricane strength.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The following day, at 21:00 UTC, Kenneth was declared post-tropical.</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Lidia">Tropical Storm Lidia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Lidia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Lidia 2017-08-31 2023Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/150px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg" width="150" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/225px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg/300px-Lidia_2017-08-31_2023Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6734" data-file-height="9706" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Lidia_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Lidia 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/150px-Lidia_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/225px-Lidia_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Lidia_2017_track.png/300px-Lidia_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>August 31&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 3</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>65&#160;mph (100&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 987&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)">Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)</a></div>\n<p>On August 29, the NHC monitored a potential area of Tropical Cyclone development near the coast of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Watch">Tropical Storm Watches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Watch" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Watch">Hurricane Watches</a> stretching from <a href="/wiki/Todos_Santos,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Todos Santos, Baja California Sur">Todos Santos</a> to <a href="/wiki/Los_Barriles,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Los Barriles, Baja California Sur">Los Barriles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">The NHC initiated advisories on Tropical Storm Lidia at 00:00 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August 31 about 180&#160;mi (290&#160;km) south-southeast of the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>. Favorable conditions allowed Lidia to intensify, and by 21:00 UTC on August 31, the storm peaked with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 65&#160;mph (100&#160;km/h) and a minimum <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a> of 987 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (29.1 <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">inHg</a>). Around 12:00 UTC on the following day, Lidia made <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> near <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Chale" title="Puerto Chale">Puerto Chale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a>, at the same intensity. The cyclone weakened significantly while traversing the mountainous terrain of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a>, and by early on September 2, deep convection was mainly limited to a few strong clusters near the center. Around that time, Lidia briefly moved offshore, before making another landfall near <a href="/wiki/Punta_Abreojos" title="Punta Abreojos">Punta Abreojos</a> a few hours later. By that time, Lidia had weakened steadily, and emerged over the Pacific Ocean on September 2. However, Lidia continued to weaken due to cold <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperatures" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea surface temperatures">sea surface temperatures</a>. After failing to produce deep convection for about 12\xe2\x80\x9315 hours, the NHC declared that Lidia had degenerated into a remnant low-pressure area at 09:00 UTC on September 2 about 40&#160;mi (65&#160;km/h) southwest of Punta Baja, Baja California.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Otis">Hurricane Otis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Otis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Otis 2017-09-17 1915Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/150px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg" width="150" height="208" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/225px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg/300px-Otis_2017-09-17_1915Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5754" data-file-height="7987" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Otis_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Otis 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/150px-Otis_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/225px-Otis_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Otis_2017_track.png/300px-Otis_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 11&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 19</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 965&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On September 8, <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Katia" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Katia</a> of the Atlantic made landfall on Mexico, dissipating on September 9. However, its mid-level circulation survived, and eventually spawned an area of low pressure off the coast of Mexico. On September 11, the system organized into Tropical Depression Fifteen-E. During the next several days, the depression slowly drifted westward, before strengthening into Tropical Storm Otis on September 16. While only marginal strengthening was forecast, Otis unexpectedly rapidly intensified into a Category 2 hurricane by 17:00 UTC on September 17, despite lower ocean temperatures, drier air, and increased wind shear.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> Otis continued to intensify into a Category 3 major hurricane by 03:00 UTC on September 18, developing a well-defined eye with a diameter of 10 nautical miles (12&#160;mi; 19&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> By 21:00 UTC on September 18, Otis had rapidly degenerated back into a tropical storm with maximum sustained winds of 40 knots (46&#160;mph; 74&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Twelve hours after developing a well-defined eye, Otis started weakening at a remarkable rate, losing most of its deep convection from low ocean surface temperatures until it became a remnant low on September 19, due to a lack of convection.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Max">Hurricane Max</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hurricane Max">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Max 2017-09-14 1705Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/150px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg" width="150" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/225px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg/300px-Max_2017-09-14_1705Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7475" data-file-height="10753" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Max_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Max 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/150px-Max_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/225px-Max_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Max_2017_track.png/300px-Max_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 13&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 15</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>85&#160;mph (140&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 985&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On September&#160;9, the NHC mentioned the possibility for an area of low pressure to form south of Mexico over later days.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> A trough of low pressure materialized the next day,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> steadily organizing into a tropical depression near the southwestern coast of Mexico around 15:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;13. Despite forecasts of little or no intensification,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> the newly formed cyclone intensified into Tropical Storm Max six hours later.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> Quick intensification ensued as the storm improved in structure and developed a well-defined eye, prompting the NHC to upgrade Max to a hurricane around 12:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;14.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> After attaining peak winds of 85&#160;mph (140&#160;km/h),<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> the hurricane moved ashore the coastline of Guerrero at a slightly reduced strength around 21:00&#160;UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> The mountainous terrain of inland Mexico severely disrupted Max\'s circulation, causing it to degenerate by 09:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;15.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In preparation for Max, about 788 people evacuated to temporary shelters.<sup id="cite_ref-ElManana_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElManana-131">[129]</a></sup> Throughout Guerrero, over 1,500 homes were inundated by floodwaters or damaged by strong winds that ripped off roofs. Over 100 trees were downed, mudslides and sinkholes closed several roads (including <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Federal_Highway_200" title="Mexican Federal Highway 200">Mexican Federal Highway 200</a>), and telephone service was cut. At the height of the storm, 126,503 <a href="/wiki/Comisi%C3%B3n_Federal_de_Electricidad" title="Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Electricidad">Comisi\xc3\xb3n Federal de Electricidad</a> customers lost electricity. A bridge between <a href="/wiki/Cruz_Grande" title="Cruz Grande">Cruz Grande</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copala,_Guerrero" title="Copala, Guerrero">Copala</a> was severely damaged, and access to <a href="/wiki/Juchit%C3%A1n_de_Zaragoza" title="Juchit\xc3\xa1n de Zaragoza">Juchit\xc3\xa1n de Zaragoza</a> was severed due to a flooded highway. One of 17 rapidly-rising rivers swept away a residence and two neighbors who attempted to rescue the homeowner; one of the neighbors died, constituting one of two deaths attributed to the storm. At least 3,000 residents across five municipalities in Guerrero were stranded.<sup id="cite_ref-ElManana_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElManana-131">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Waves of 10\xe2\x80\x9316&#160;ft (3\xe2\x80\x935&#160;m) battered the coastline, where six ships were sunk.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Norma">Hurricane Norma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Norma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1&#160;hurricane&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Norma 2017-09-15 2055Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/150px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg" width="150" height="210"
