srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/225px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg/300px-Norma_2017-09-15_2055Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5583" data-file-height="7823" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Norma_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Norma 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/150px-Norma_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/225px-Norma_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Norma_2017_track.png/300px-Norma_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 14&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 20</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>75&#160;mph (120&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 985&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On September 10, the NHC started to monitor an area of low pressure well south of <a href="/wiki/Manzanillo,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Manzanillo, Mexico">Manzanillo, Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> The disturbance gradually organized during the following days and by 09:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;14 the system was noted to develop a well-defined center and spiral banding.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> This led to the formation of Tropical Storm Norma, skipping tropical depression status.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> The newly formed tropical storm continued to intensify at a steady pace while it moved slowly northward, becoming a category 1 hurricane by 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;16 and reaching winds of 75&#160;mph (120&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> At this time warnings were being required for the southern portions of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> as Norma was forecast to become a major hurricane and make landfall in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> However, its broad circulation and the entrainment of dry air quickly became an impediment in doing so.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> Norma then weakened back to a tropical storm at 21:00&#160;UTC later that day while becoming stationary, though a developing ridge over <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> began to move the storm slowly towards the north.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> Norma maintained its intensity the next day and continued being slowly steered by the ridge towards a northwesterly to west-northwesterly path, all tropical storm warnings were discontinued as Norma started to shift its track more to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The cyclone continued weakening for several days as it slowly drifted to the west, until finally being declared a remnant low at 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Pilar">Tropical Storm Pilar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Pilar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pilar 2017-09-24 1740Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/150px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg" width="150" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/225px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg/300px-Pilar_2017-09-24_1740Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4400" data-file-height="5600" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Pilar_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Pilar 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/150px-Pilar_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/225px-Pilar_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Pilar_2017_track.png/300px-Pilar_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>September 23&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 September 25</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1002&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>During the week of September 18, the NHC began monitoring a tropical wave,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> as it spawned a broad area of low pressure located offshore of the southwestern coast of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> The disturbance lacked any significant organization until September 23 at around 21:00&#160;UTC when the system was noted to developed surface winds of over 35&#160;mph (55&#160;km/h) becoming Tropical Depression Eighteen-E.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> The depression organized into a tropical storm six hours later and was given the name <i>Pilar</i>, the sixteenth named storm of the annual Pacific hurricane season.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> Thereafter, despite having a disorganized appearance on satellite, Pilar\'s winds increased in strength, and it reached its peak with sustained winds of 45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup> By 09:00&#160;UTC on September 24, Pilar continued to track north along the coast, with warnings being issued for the southwestern coast of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> However, early on September 25, these warnings were discontinued,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> as Tropical Storm Pilar showed signs of weakening mainly due to land interaction, and was reduced to a tropical depression before ultimately dissipating at around 21:00&#160;UTC later that same day.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> Although Pilar did not make landfall as a tropical cyclone, heavy rainfall was reported in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Vallarta,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Vallarta, Mexico">Puerto Vallarta, Mexico</a>, northeast of <a href="/wiki/Islas_Mar%C3%ADas" title="Islas Mar\xc3\xadas">Islas Mar\xc3\xadas</a> and in other areas along the Mexican coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Ramon">Tropical Storm Ramon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Ramon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm&#160;(SSHWS)</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ramon 2017-10-04 1945Z.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/150px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg" width="150" height="198" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/225px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg/300px-Ramon_2017-10-04_1945Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6721" data-file-height="8865" /></a><span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/File:Ramon_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="Ramon 2017 track.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/150px-Ramon_2017_track.png" width="150" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/225px-Ramon_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ramon_2017_track.png/300px-Ramon_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1854" /></a></span></div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Duration</th>\n<td>October 4&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 October 5</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>\n<td>45&#160;mph (75&#160;km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>&#160; 1002&#160;<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>On October 3, the NHC noted a high chance of tropical development in an area of low pressure, to the south of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> The system increased in intensity and became Tropical Storm Ramon early on October 4, skipping tropical depression status.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> Due to wind shear from a large anticyclone to its north, the storm did not intensify much further.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> Although it was forecast to linger over open waters as it moved westward, this did not occur and the system quickly grew disorganized.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> Ramon weakened into a tropical depression later on the same day, having only lasted as a tropical storm for 18 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> As it moved westward, Ramon continued to weaken, until it finally degenerated into a trough of low pressure and the National Hurricane Center issued its last advisory on the degenerated system at 09:00&#160;UTC on October 5.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>\n<p>The following names will be used for named storms that form in the northeastern Pacific Ocean during 2017. <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Pacific hurricane names">Retired names</a>, if any, will be announced by the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> in the spring of 2018. The names not retired from this list will be used again in the 2023 season.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> This same list was used in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2011 Pacific hurricane season">2011 season</a>.</p>\n<table width="90%">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li>Adrian</li>\n<li>Beatriz</li>\n<li>Calvin</li>\n<li>Dora</li>\n<li>Eugene</li>\n<li>Fernanda</li>\n<li>Greg</li>\n<li>Hilary</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li>Irwin</li>\n<li>Jova</li>\n<li>Kenneth</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Lidia_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Lidia (2017)">Lidia</a></li>\n<li>Max</li>\n<li>Norma</li>\n<li>Otis</li>\n<li>Pilar</li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li>Ramon</li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Selma&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Todd&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Veronica&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Wiley&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Xina&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">York&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Zelda&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>For storms that form in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>\'s area of responsibility, encompassing the area between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140 degrees west</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, all names are used in a series of <a href="/wiki/List_of_tropical_cyclone_names#Central_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tropical cyclone names">four rotating lists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> The next four names slated for use are shown below.</p>\n<table style="width:90%;">\n<tr>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Walaka&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Akoni&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Ema&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul>\n<li><span style="color:#666666">Hone&#160;<i>(unused)</i></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>The usage of the Atlantic storm name "Don", and the name "Hilary", in July garnered some negative attention relating to <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">United States President</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, and former Presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>. People also took to Twitter to poke fun at the names and both individuals, with political jokes.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2017 Pacific hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, landfall(s), denoted in parentheses, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2017 USD.</p>\n<table align="center" border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A major hurricane is a storm that ranks as Category&#160;3 or higher on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm\'s intensity of over 33&#160;knots (38&#160;mph, 61&#160;km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2017_Pacific_hurricane_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2017 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs">Talk:2017 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-season-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-season_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation report">Dorst Neal. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101206195446/http://www.aoml.noaa.gov/hrd/tcfaq/G1.html">When is hurricane season?</a> (Report).
